## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is central to constitutive modeling of thermomechanical behavior of materials. Typical effects include elastic and plastic strain response, thermal softening, and possibly thermal expansion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity with thermal expansion: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (basic thermoelastic stress)
- Thermal expansion offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress due to thermal expansion mismatch)
- Power‑law strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (basic Ramberg‑Osgood type)
- Ludwik hardening law: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power‑law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation of flow stress with strain)
- Voce with temperature‑dependent saturation: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * exp(-c3 * T)
- Exponential thermal softening of yield stress: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature‑dependent yield + strain hardening)
- Multiplicative thermal softening on strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power‑law strain hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Johnson‑Cook‑like thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (simple linear temperature factor on flow stress)
- Temperature‑dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linearly varying Young’s modulus)
- Exponential modulus change: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (exponentially decreasing stiffness with temperature)
- Coupling via product of independent functions: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T)**c3 (power‑law strain hardening with power‑law thermal softening)
- Yield plus thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 * exp(-c4 * T) (separate thermal effects on yield and hardening)
- Saturation strain with temperature shift: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * (epsilon + c2 * T))) (temperature modifying the rate of saturation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic response → stress proportional to strain (sigma = c0 * epsilon), often modulated by temperature
- Strain hardening (plastic flow) → stress increases with strain as a power law (epsilon**c) or saturating exponential (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening → stress decreases with increasing temperature, commonly modelled with exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*T)
- Yield stress → a constant additive term (c0) that may itself soften with temperature
- Thermal expansion → strain enters as (epsilon - c*T) to account for temperature‑induced strain mismatch
- Multiplicative separability → overall stress often written as f(epsilon) * g(T) when hardening and softening are independent
- Saturation of flow stress → sigma approaches a finite limit as strain increases, captured by c0 - c1*exp(-c2*epsilon) or similar bounded forms
- Linear temperature dependence of modulus → stiffness varies linearly with T, appearing as (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon
